< review>
Decent craft beer selection for beer lovers.  Nice contemporary bar atmosphere to sit down, grab a couple of drinks and have some great food.  The pretzel bites are amazing with the sea salt and the beer cheese sauce.  It was so good they need to have a larger size serving for bigger groups honestly one person alone can eat that appetizer.  Had the bacon and blue cheese salad.  Great salad and super fresh blue cheese dressing totally made the salad.  Ordered the meat pizza it was pretty good too.  Coming back to try the calzone next time.  Glad Madera has a place like this to grab an adult drink and a bite to eat.</review>

< review>
A woman T-boned me and I needed body repair. Everyone was very helpful and friendly but I'll be damned if it didn't take nearly a month to get my car back (Feb. 18 thru March 14 judging by my emails).

My preliminary estimate said 8 days. Well, once they started taking it apart they realized they don't know anything about this car (Honda Clarity Plug-in). A few weeks later and a couple separate rounds of ordering parts and waiting for them to arrive, I finally got it back. But not until three days after it was done, because I received no email updates and they only left one voicemail. Anyone who has an iPhone knows that you only get 1 notification per voicemail message, if you're lucky to get one at all. They should have called multiple times with how long they took. To add insult to injury, my insurance and the rental car wanted me to pay for the 3 extra days that I didn't know my car was done. I never paid it, and if I get a collection notice I'll be forwarding it to the repair shop.

They are the first collision shop on the list of approved repair shops with my Farmers agent. So it makes sense they would be the busiest. But that was nuts.

"SLO" is a way of life and not a good one. If you want your car back fast, go with a shop that seems confident with how long it's going to take to repair it.</review>

<Text>7/17/13

Right before arriving at Playland-Not-At-The-Beach, my husband had a sudden craving for chicken that he HAD to satisfy. Weird.

There were 3 of us in the car and none had ever been to a Church's before. The drive-thru was like any other, but the menu was new to me! I wasn't at all hungry but I had to try SOMETHING! So I tried the Cajun rice (side) and one piece of crispy chicken. Husband had a chicken sandwich with fries and a drink. Food came pretty quick and I asked for hot sauce, but it was already in the bag. Sweet. Wish I had a couple extra packets. It was pretty good stuff!  My piece of chicken was crunchy and good. I liked the crispy breading but it was a little greasy for me after a few bites. Good flavor though. I don't know how to explain the cajun rice. It was like a mash of rice and meat. We all agreed there was meat in the rice. It's probably my fault for not knowing that cajun rice has meat, but I didn't want unidentifiable meat (or any meat for that matter) in my rice so I tossed this.

Husband's sandwich lasted about as long as my rice. He took a few bites and then took a look inside. The patty just looked really unappetizing. It was a grey-ish color in the middle and something just wasn't right.  His fries ended up in my lap at this point as he tried to wash away all the bad with his giant soda. I decided to abandon my piece of chicken after viewing his. I'd return here, but only for the hot sauce.</Text><Name>Amy Palmer<//Name><Rate>2< /Rate><Pics>None</Pics><Response>None<//Response><gmap_id>0x80857851b0e45d77:0xfb3a73c52a5be6ce< /gmap_id></record>

< Review>
Great hike, about an hour at a slow pace to the summit with fantastic views. The top as a  military air force electronics station. Condor viewing areas. From the top another trail drops down into the valley where it intersects with other trails leading to Grouss mtn and Cerro Noreste (Abel Mountain trail). We have seen bear who usually head for the campgrounds to raid the trash bins. Deer are also common on the mountain if your quiet.<//Review>

<user_name>Cameron Embree</user_name><Time>1525049505565</Time>< rating>
5<//rating>
< review>
Easy trail for someone with a little hiking experience and easy to moderate for someone with no experience. Trailhead is a bit of a drive up a road some people take too fast and can have rocks on it. Drive slow and safe. The trail had a little snow around but the temperature was light jacket worthy until you got going. Two good viewing points, one at the top of Pinos and another on a trail that starts at the top of Pinos.< /review>

<review>Awesome place to just play in the snow without any restrictions. Will need snow chains to get up there though so make sure to buy some prior to your trip or if you're lucky to found some available they do sell them at the Ace Hardware store in Frazier Park or at the bottom of Frazier Mountain Park Rd next to the AM PM. You will need a one day Adventure Pass to park which can be bought at Big 5 or other sporting good store for only $5 but they do sell them at certain stores and shops in Frazier Park too. You can purchase a year pass as well, good to all California national parks. Make sure to take trash bags to pick up after yourself because there are no trash cans up there just a couple of dumpsters.</review>< rate>
5</rate>

4< /Rating>
< text>
This park appears to have real potential. Toddler playground, big-kids playground, lots of grass and near the water so a little cooler than inland Hayward. Also, it is not near busy streets, so letting the kids run around free on the grass would not worry me. There are a lot of wild geese and other birds here, which likely amounts to a lot of bird poop in the grass. Is also really close to the bay, meaning that it is far from any freeways or even Hesperian blvd. But a nice looking park nonetheless.< /text>

< Text>
I expect to be able to rate this 5 stars when they finish construction because it looks like it will be better than ever, but right now(jan 2017) half the park is a closed construction area. The dog park, playground, restrooms,soccer field and basketball courts are all open as well as the community center.  In the construction area at this point there is a new duck pond with picnic tables around it . New restrooms, New basketball courts, New parking areas, and the beginning of new baseball fields.
Jan 2018 update..updating stars and ranking. New area is open and very nice. A great kids playground including a zip line. New restrooms and basketball courts. Elevated composition "wiid" walkways around new Duck pond with a gazebo overlooking the water and picnic tables. All walkways smooth and wheelchair accessible.  Drive in access from via Catherine now open also in addition the the Buena visa entrance.</Text>

<Rate>3</Rate><Text>When i first moved here 4 years ago the place had a poorly kept fountain/pond and was infested with waterfowl. The pathway littered with droppings as well as the surrounding grass area.  And i swear on my life there was a dead beaver or muskrat or some kind of gopher that bloated from being submerged and left to rot jn the sun sitting belly up shore side of the east side of the fountain/pond. Needless to say that was the only time we really went there. I just wanted to see the park my HOA fee paid for.

Flash forward a couple years or so and they took that damn pond out and put up some new baseball/softball fields and other things and the waterfowl up and left now leaving a seemingly easier to maintain park and I feel less swindled

One thing I have to say not having kids yet myself the only reason I go to the park is for the dog park area and my 2 dogs. The dog park itself is a small chain linked fenced off area with a few picnic tables. A bunch of pot holes on the left side and tanbark which fence of as this writing is in minor disrepair. Also the water fountain is inconviently placed a good walk away and what they do provide is those $3 buckets from home depot filled with water from god knows when. At the risk of sounded snobby, I don't let my dogs drink from them. It'd be nice if they included dog friendly water fountains which I know would cost money and irrigation but from reading the San Lorenzo briefs they spent $53,000 to refurbish the village hall bathrooms, $10,410 to update the computer database which I don't even understand what that is and needs $10k for. It cost $2,290 to replace the office flourescent lights and I could've picked up a bunch of $20 one from my Uncle in law. A lot of this stuff seems to be for the office and its workers and when I compare that to what the spent on the village general it seems like they got more. What I'm saying is an updated dog park would've been nice as well.

There's so much unused field it could be extended a bit and it'd be nice to have the dog friendly fountains and maybe the nice buffer, entrance area to leash or unleash your dog before you enter the park and make it harder for the more enthusiatic dogs from jolting out.< /Text>< pictures>
